At the bus stop, 82 children got on the bus, and some children got off, leaving a total of 30 children on the bus.\n\nLet's calculate how many children got off the bus:\n\n1. After 82 children got on, the total number of children on the bus would be 28 + 82 = 110.\n2. Since there are 30 children on the bus after some got off, the number of children who got off is 110 - 30 = 80.\n\nNow, we need to find out how many more children got on the bus than those who got off:\n\n82 children got on the bus, and 80 children got off. Therefore, 82 - 80 = 2 more children got on the bus than those who got off.\n\nThe answer is 2."

Now, there are 8 action figures on the shelf. \n\nLet's denote the number of action figures Jerry added as \\( x \\).\n\nThe equation representing the situation is:\n\\[ 7 + x - 10 = 8 \\]\n\nSolving for \\( x \\):\n\\[ 7 + x - 10 = 8 \\]\n\\[ x - 3 = 8 \\]\n\\[ x = 8 + 3 \\]\n\\[ x = 11 \\]\n\nJerry added 11 action figures to the shelf. "Initially, Nell had 309 baseball cards and 356 Ace cards, which totals to 309 + 356 = 665 cards. After giving some cards to Jeff, she has 415 cards left. This means she gave away 665 - 415 = 250 cards.\n\nTo find out how many more baseball cards than Ace cards Nell has now, we need to determine the current number of each type of card. Let's assume she gave away \\( x \\) baseball cards and \\( y \\) Ace cards, with \\( x + y = 250 \\).\n\nThe number of baseball cards Nell has now is \\( 309 - x \\), and the number of Ace cards is \\( 356 - y \\).\n\nWe need to find the difference between the number of baseball cards and Ace cards Nell has now:\n\n\\[\n(309 - x) - (356 - y) = 415 - 356 = 59\n\\]\n\nThis equation simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n309 - x - 356 + y = 59\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny - x = 59 - 47\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny - x = -47\n\\]\n\nThis means Nell has 47 more Ace cards than baseball cards. However, since we are looking for how many more baseball cards than Ace cards she has, we need to take the absolute value:\n\n\\[\nx - y = 47\n\\]\n\nTherefore, Nell has 47 more baseball cards than Ace cards. The answer is 47."

"Initially, there were 36 children on the bus. At the bus stop, 68 children got off the bus. After some children got on the bus, there were 12 children in total.\n\nFirst, let's determine how many children got on the bus. If 68 children got off, then the number of children remaining on the bus before any got on would be:\n\n36 - 68 = -32\n\nSince it's not possible to have a negative number of children, this means that more children got on the bus to reach a total of 12 children. Therefore, the number of children who got on the bus is:\n\n12 - (-32) = 12 + 32 = 44\n\nNow, we need to find out how many more children got off the bus than those who got on:\n\n68 (got off) - 44 (got on) = 24\n\nSo, 24 more children got off the bus than those who got on. The answer is 24."

"To find the length of Jesse's room, we can use the formula for the area of a rectangle, which is:\n\n\\[ \\text{Area} = \\text{Width} \\times \\text{Length} \\]\n\nWe know the area of the carpet needed is 10 square feet, and the width of the room is 2 feet. To find out how much Edward had before he spent his money, we can set up the equation:\n\nLet \\( x \\) be the amount of money Edward had initially.\n\n1. He spent $17, so he had \\( x - 17 \\).\n2. He received $10, so he had \\( x - 17 + 10 \\).\n3. Now he has $7, so \\( x - 17 + 10 = 7 \\).\n\nSimplifying the equation:\n\n\\( x - 7 = 7 \\)\n\nAdding 7 to both sides:\n\n\\( x = 14 \\)\n\nSo, Edward had $14 before he spent his money. The answer is 14.'

"Let's denote the number of marbles Doug originally had as \\( D \\). According to the problem, Ed had 2 more marbles than Doug, so Ed originally had \\( D + 2 \\) marbles.\n\nAfter Doug lost some marbles, Ed has 19 more marbles than Doug. This means that the number of marbles Doug has now is \\( D - x \\), where \\( x \\) is the number of marbles Doug lost.\n\nThe equation representing the current situation is:\n\n\\[ D + 2 = (D - x) + 19 \\]\n\nSimplifying the equation:\n\n\\[ D + 2 = D - x + 19 \\]\n\nSubtract \\( D \\) from both sides:\n\n\\[ 2 = -x + 19 \\]\n\nSubtract 19 from both sides:\n\n\\[ 2 - 19 = -x \\]\n\n\\[ -17 = -x \\]\n\nMultiply both sides by -1:\n\n\\[ x = 17 \\]\n\nSo, Doug lost 17 marbles. The answer is 17."

To find out how much more carpet she needs, we subtract the carpet she already has from the total area of the room:\n\n\\[ 165 \\, \\text{square feet} - 16 \\, \\text{square feet} = 149 \\, \\text{square feet} \\]\n\nJesse needs 149 more square feet of carpet to cover the whole floor. "Let's break down the problem step by step:\n\n1. Let the number of apples Jackie has be \\( x \\).\n2. Adam has 4 more apples than Jackie, so Adam has \\( x + 4 \\) apples.\n3. Together, Adam and Jackie have 14 apples: \n   \\[\n   x + (x + 4) = 14\n   \\]\n4. Simplifying the equation:\n   \\[\n   2x + 4 = 14\n   \\]\n5. Subtract 4 from both sides:\n   \\[\n   2x = 10\n   \\]\n6. Divide by 2:\n   \\[\n   x = 5\n   \\]\n   So, Jackie has 5 apples, and Adam has \\( 5 + 4 = 9 \\) apples.\n\n7. Together, Adam and Jackie have \\( 5 + 9 = 14 \\) apples, which matches the given information.\n\n8. Bob has 6 more apples than Adam and Jackie together:\n   \\[\n   14 + 6 = 20\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, Bob has 20 apples. The answer is 20."

Since the recipe calls for 6 cups of flour, she has already put in some flour, but we need to find out how many more cups she needs to add to reach 21 cups. \n\nIf she needs 21 cups in total and the recipe calls for 6 cups, she needs to add 21 - 6 = 15 more cups of flour. \n\nThe answer is 15.'

'Initially, there were 21 roses in the vase. Jessica threw away 34 roses, which means she removed more roses than were originally in the vase. To find out how many roses she cut from her garden, we can set up the equation:\n\nInitial roses - thrown away roses + new roses = current roses\n\n21 - 34 + new roses = 15\n\nSolving for the new roses:\n\nnew roses = 15 - (21 - 34)\nnew roses = 15 - (-13)\nnew roses = 15 + 13\nnew roses = 28\n\nJessica cut 28 new roses from her garden. To find out how many more roses she threw away than she cut, we subtract the number of new roses from the number of roses she threw away:\n\n34 (thrown away) - 28 (cut) = 6\n\nJessica threw away 6 more roses than she cut from her garden. The answer is 6.'

"To find the width of Jesse's room, we can use the formula for the area of a rectangle, which is length multiplied by width. We know the area of the carpet is 14 square feet and the length of the room is 7 feet. \n\nLet's denote the width of the room as \\( w \\). The equation for the area is:\n\n\\[ 7 \\times w = 14 \\]\n\nTo find \\( w \\), divide both sides of the equation by 7:\n\n\\[ w = \\frac{14}{7} = 2 \\]\n\nSo, the width of Jesse's room is 2 feet. The answer is 2."

To find out how many ripe apples the tree had initially, we add the number of ripe apples Rachel picked to the number of ripe apples currently on the tree: \n\n3 (picked) + 2 (remaining) = 5 ripe apples.\n\nThe tree had 5 ripe apples to begin with. The answer is 5.'
'To find out how many points Melissa scored in 79 games, we need to calculate the total points she earned from both regular and bonus points in each game.\n\nFirst, calculate the total points per game:\n- Regular points per game: 109\n- Bonus points per game: 82\n\nTotal points per game = 109 + 82 = 191\n\nNow, multiply the total points per game by the number of games:\nTotal points in 79 games = 191 × 79\n\n191 × 79 = 15,089\n\nTherefore, Melissa scored a total of 15,089 points in 79 games. The answer is 15,089.'
'Rachel had 7 pages of math homework and 4 pages of reading homework. To find out how many more pages of math homework she had than reading homework, we subtract the number of reading homework pages from the number of math homework pages: 7 - 4 = 3. Therefore, Rachel had 3 more pages of math homework than reading homework. The answer is 3.'
"First, we need to determine Dean's height. We know that Ron is 15 feet tall and Dean is 6 feet shorter than Ron. Therefore, Dean's height is 15 - 6 = 9 feet.\n\nThe depth of the water is 9 times Dean's height. So, the depth of the water is 9 * 9 = 81 feet.\n\nThe answer is 81 feet."
'To find the total number of pupils in the school, we need to add the number of girls and boys together. There are 308 girls and 318 boys. \n\nSo, the total number of pupils is 308 + 318 = 626.\n\nThe answer is 626.'
'Katie has 63 DS games, and her friends have 57 games. To find out how many more games Katie has than her friends, we subtract the number of games her friends have from the number of games Katie has: 63 - 57 = 6. Therefore, Katie has 6 more games than her friends. The answer is 6.'
'Luke scored a total of 84 points after playing 2 rounds of a trivia game. If he gained the same number of points each round, we can find out how many points he scored per round by dividing the total points by the number of rounds. \n\n84 points ÷ 2 rounds = 42 points per round.\n\nThe answer is 42.'
'He needs a total of 353 grams of wax for the feathers and requires 22 grams more. This means he already has 353 - 22 = 331 grams of wax. The answer is 331.'
"It seems there is a mistake in the problem statement. The number of seeds that grew into flowers in each flower bed (58) is greater than the total number of seeds planted (36), which is not possible. Let's address the problem with the information given:\n\nPaige and her mom planted a total of 36 seeds, and they put 12 seeds in each flower bed. To find out how many flower beds they had, we divide the total number of seeds by the number of seeds per flower bed:\n\n36 seeds ÷ 12 seeds per flower bed = 3 flower beds.\n\nTherefore, they had 3 flower beds. The answer is 3."

'Mary needs a total of 7 cups of sugar for the recipe. She has already added 4 cups of sugar. Therefore, she needs to add 7 - 4 = 3 more cups of sugar. The answer is 3.'
"The problem states that the grasshopper jumped 13 inches and that the grasshopper jumped 2 inches farther than the frog. This seems to be a mistake in the problem statement, as it should specify that the frog jumped 2 inches farther than the grasshopper. Assuming the frog jumped 2 inches farther than the grasshopper, we can calculate the frog's jump as follows:\n\nGrasshopper's jump = 13 inches\nFrog's jump = Grasshopper's jump + 2 inches = 13 inches + 2 inches = 15 inches\n\nTherefore, the frog jumped 15 inches. The answer is 15."
